Free Talk

World Miscellanea 166

— Sea Guest

A certain British scientist claims to know the height of ancient humans. It only requires measuring one or two of their skeletal remains to find out.

American farmers are the wealthiest in the world. There are 6.5 million people who own their own farms and cultivate or raise livestock, and most of them own cars to transport their crops.

Queen Mary's Needlework Guild in London once held an exhibition that included six woolen shawls hand-knitted by Prince Edward and Prince George.

The Paris Police Department has collected the most criminal fingerprints, totaling 1,727,000 types. All the police departments in the world cannot match it.

The British electrical industry is exceptionally developed. A total of 180,000 to 200,000 people across the country rely on electricity to maintain their lives.

All public entertainment venues in London must close at 10:00 PM every night, except that Westminster and Holborn are allowed to extend one hour because these two places are entertainment centers.

In 1928, the British government's expenditure on banquets totaled £11,300. One banquet to entertain the King of Egypt cost £291, and one to entertain the King of Iraq cost £817.

A Record of the Michigan Spring Banquet Amidst the Misty Wind and Rain 167

— Pu Cang

What is the magnificent new building on Weihaiwei Road? It is the Central Society (中社) organized by the core members from the sea. On the evening of days gone by, the University of Michigan Alumni Association held a gathering here. Although the weather was not good, with wind and rain swirling about, the event was still well-attended by many talented people, both young and old. How can one not record this? That night, anyone driving past the entrance of the Central Society could see a seal-script plaque with English annotations fluttering in the wind and rain. The inscription read "University of Michigan Spring Gathering," and the annotation was "A Day of Wolverines in China." A "wolverine" is the name of a voracious animal and a special product of the state of Michigan in North America, hence people from that state often use it as another name for themselves. It is commonly used in sporting events or ball games. Those on the sea have not seen this before. The architecture of the Central Society is exquisite, and the furnishings are particularly artistic. Many works by Wang Yachen, who draws on the past while lingering in France, were displayed. In terms of traditional Chinese paintings, there were many old works from the Former Cold Friend Painting Association, such as Yi Yuanjing's bamboo and rocks, Chen Shuren's flowers and birds, He Xiangning's plum blossoms, Li Qiujun and Li Zuhán's green and blue landscapes, and Zheng Wuchang and Qian Shouting's ink paintings, all outstanding figures of their time. As the silver lamps were lit, Chen Tingrui immediately brought his young son along. Before long, male and female classmates had arrived in droves. There were quite a few people who "brought in husband and wife." Foreign classmates attending the meeting included American Consul General E. S. Cunningham, American Court Prosecutor in China Dr. Sellet, Japanese Commercial Counselor to China Kan Seimatsu, and St. John's University Professor P. B. Sullivan. As the clock struck seven, Chairman Chen Tingrui announced the start of the dinner. The seating was arranged in a U-shape, and the table was decorated with yellow and blue paper ribbons, forming an M-shape. It was as natural as a school badge of the U of M. Wu Jingxiong arrived last and repeatedly praised this application of fine arts in practice. After the chairman's opening remarks, Cunningham delivered a speech first. As he stood up, everyone watched and cheered, congratulating him on his continued vigor despite his age and his recent election. The order of events included a "age test" as a form of entertainment. Prizes were given to the oldest and youngest attendees. The oldest received a four-foot vertical scroll painting of golden fruit by Yu Xueyang. The youngest received candy, also a gift from Yu Xueyang. Cunningham graduated from Michigan many years ago, more than twenty years ago. Although he did not appear decrepit, his gold-flecked frosted temples and completely bald head already told people of his advanced age and status among his peers. His speech was mainly about historical anecdotes, which could be used as a reference for studying the history of the development of the United States. Michigan is located between the eastern and western United States and is extremely rich in natural resources. At that time, it was very difficult to travel from the east to the west, similar to traveling from China to the United States now. The University of Michigan has contributed greatly to the prosperity of the western United States today. He also said that the famous American warship S.S. Houston from the European War is now docked in Shanghai and plans to send invitations to alumni to visit. Next, Sellet delivered a speech that was extremely humorous. He said that he saw former apprentices sitting at the table, so although he could not compare to Cunningham as a first-generation graduate, he was still a second-generation graduate. The crowd laughed for a long time. Some people called out, "A grand meeting of three generations, a grand meeting!" He also mentioned that University of Michigan alumni have made great political contributions in recent years, such as the fact that there were as many as four cabinet members during President Coolidge's era. Following him, Sullivan spoke. He was good at sports, especially basketball, so he was able to give a systematic report on the championship situation of various sports at Michigan during the year, such as track and field, football, basketball, baseball, indoor sports, ice sports, and swimming, in an organized and orderly manner. However, there were many fraternity members who had recently been fined for violating the alcohol prohibition, which was also an interesting anecdote. Finally, Wu Jingxiong spoke, using extremely amusing jokes to adjust the psychology of the crowd and elicit a roar of laughter. It can be said that he was skilled in rhetoric. Immediately after, the staff was briefly elected. The event was also supported by Tianchu, Wuzhou, Weiyi, and Central factories, which provided monosodium glutamate, soap, Liangdan, and chili soy sauce as gifts. Attendees were able to leave with full loads.

A Short Note on Seeing Off the Spring 168

— Ke Ding'an

On my day off, I had half a day of leisure and visited Mengrong. It was exactly half past eight, and Mengrong had already been working for some time. His female student, Madam Ma, wife of Zhu Qizhan, asked him to revise her draft. She was also early. The paintings were three pieces, including azaleas, etc. The brushwork closely resembled Mengrong's and did not seem like the work of a woman. I heard that she had only been studying painting for half a year, but her achievements were already remarkable. I invited Mengrong for a stroll in Zhaofeng Park. On this day, Mr. Zhu invited Mengrong for a stroll in Zhaofeng Park. Madam Ma had finished revising the draft and went ahead, saying that she would come to pick us up in a car. Mengrong painted a willow and swallow for me. The old willow was dancing, and the swallows were flying. The description of the scenery was wonderful, right down to the tip of the brush. Suddenly, I saw a picture of strange fish hanging on the wall. It depicted several peculiar fish, with lively expressions, reminiscent of Zhuangzi by the Hao River. Zhao Huishu had similar works in the past, and Mengrong was no less skilled. Mengrong has a book called "Ink Fun," which specifically discusses the use of ink as the use of color. The wonderful fun is endless and can be a model. "Spectrum of Grass Insects, Fish, and Crabs": First, depict the shape; second, depict the spirit; third, depict the intention. Use straight lines as the foundation and beauty as the ultimate goal. The publication of these two books will benefit future students. How shallow could they be?

Mr. Zhu arrived in his car, and we went together. Ms. Jin Qijing was also in the car, and she and Mengrong were talking about the current Sino-Japanese Painting Exhibition. Their enthusiasm was extremely high. The car traveled very quickly, and we arrived in an instant. Upon entering, the fragrant aroma filled my nostrils, almost intoxicating me. I jokingly said to Mengrong, "We are in the hustle and bustle of everyday life, burying our heads in work, and we don't know when it is spring or when it is summer. We only know that there is a difference between cold and warm, but there is no great difference. Now, looking at this beautiful park, with its lush trees and beautiful flowers and plants, I know that on the bustling Shenjiang (申江) River, there is still such a blessed place." Mengrong smiled. Most of the visitors were Westerners, in groups of three or two, with children in tow. Some were taking pictures, and some were boating (small toy sailboats, placed in the pond and moving slowly, were extremely interesting). In the dense green trees, I saw a Western woman holding a fairy tale book, surrounded by four or five children, quietly listening to her narration. The focus of Western family education is evident here. Compared to Chinese women who bring their children solely for the purpose of enjoying the park, the difference is vast. There were also four Western children acting like rascals and resisting, but they respected each other, were orderly and polite. All these things are worthy of emulation. When we got to the zoo, Mengrong quickly sketched a hawk, which was glaring and showing its ferocity. His sketch of the parrot was also quite lifelike. This bird is known for its ability to speak and was calling out "Hello, hello." He also sketched several other exotic birds. When he sketched a squirrel, everyone was surprised by its uniqueness. The squirrel's body had colors of yellow, blue, white, and black. The wonder of creation is truly unfathomable. After leaving the zoo, we walked slowly along the path, admiring the exotic grasses and rare flowers in the garden. The flower season had passed, and the special hybrid roses were as tall as people, with pale yellow petals falling. There were a few buds waiting to bloom. The willow leaves were soft and no longer had a delicate appearance. The water lilies in the pond were displaying their pure white beauty. The coming of spring, I did not see it; the passing of spring, I was able to see it. I recited Banqiao Daoren's "Bodhisattva Man" poem, "I can't keep the spring, so it goes. Where does the spring go after all? Come earlier next year. Await the trimming of the fireworks. The snow melts and spring comes again. Spring comes, and people grow old. Don't complain about the east wind. The east wind is complaining about me." I couldn't help but feel moved. Therefore, I wrote this short note on seeing off the spring and asked Mengrong and Qizhan what they thought of it.

Mei Lanfang's Groundbreaking New Film 169

— Ming Jing

Recently, the gramophone record business has been booming. Various companies are hiring theatrical specialists to handle liaison work, sound recording, and play arrangement. The best-selling discs in each company are those recorded by Mei (Lanfang) and Yu (Shuyan). However, most of the previous recordings were individual solos, which became boring after a while. Last year, Victory Company specially hired Mr. Xu Muyun to take charge of this area in order to seek progress. Mr. Xu has had many dealings with famous actors from both the North and South. It happened that Lanfang and Fuying were both performing in Shanghai at that time, so after some liaison, an agreement was reached. It was decided to record several pieces in total: "Selling Horses," "Yang Guifei," "Starting the Journey," "Teaching the Son," "Meeting of Heroes," and "Zhuliang Village." The above pieces have now been produced and are on sale. Yesterday, I bought a set (seven discs). "Selling Horses" is a duet between Mei and Miaoxiang, a descriptive passage. "Starting the Journey" is a dialogue between Mei and Xiao (Changhua), a passage about bribing the escort. "Yang Guifei" is a dialogue between Mei and Jiang, a passage about Gao Lishi reporting the alarm. "Teaching the Son" has one side with the "Nanbangzi" tune and the other side with the "Fan Xipi" tune. Although they are all Mei Lanfang's solo performances, the new tunes composed are extremely beautiful. The use of "Fan Xipi" for female roles also began with this disc by Lanfang. The duet between Xiao and Jiang in "Meeting of Heroes" and the dialogue between the Fuying father and son in "Zhuliang Village" are both extremely brilliant. Each disc is also accompanied by new and exquisite play notes to increase interest, it is said.

A Tour Around the Yellow Sea (11) 170

— Huang Yanpei

On the morning of the fifth, the train arrived in Busan. Busan is located at the southeastern tip of the Korean Peninsula, separated by the Tsushima Strait from Shimonoseki, Japan. The journey by ship takes seven or eight hours, making it very convenient for transporting goods and passengers.

The Busan Consulate General is backed by mountains and faces the sea. The flowers and trees are serene and lovely. It is a pity that the building is in disrepair, which is not only dangerous for the residents but also concerns the dignity of the nation. Consul Chen Junzheng and others led us to the top of Yongdusan Mountain, where the entire city was in view.

Busan is the main hub for the export of various goods by sea and land to the south. It ranks first among all commercial ports in Korea. The Gyeongsangnam-do Provincial Office is located here. The population is over 116,000, and there are over 42,000 Japanese, accounting for more than one-third. As mentioned earlier, Japan is moving its citizens to South Korea, and this is evidence of that.

In the evening, we boarded the train from Shimonoseki to Tokyo. The train journey took twenty hours. Along the way, there was no open space to be seen. Needless to say, the villages we passed were surrounded by flowers and trees, with a sense of beauty in their cleanliness. The most numerous type of advertisements along the way pierced my eyes: chemical factories. I saw one chemical factory after another, continuously.

The third-class car was packed with hundreds of men, women, and children, sitting upright all night. There were no loud conversations or boisterous laughter, and there was no coughing. The order was extremely good. The train attendants swept and cleaned every one or two hours. Among the police, military police, soldiers, stationmasters, conductors, ticket sellers, ticket inspectors, train attendants, and even various vendors and children, there was not a single one who was not respectful and dutiful. Their respect and politeness towards the passengers, and the corresponding courtesy of the passengers towards them, can be called unparalleled. It was as if we had entered a well-mannered household, with strict teachers and fathers above, and the children absolutely did not dare to be presumptuous. This was my fifth trip to Japan, and I had become accustomed to it. My companions, who were visiting for the first time, were especially amazed and full of praise.

The cherry blossoms along the way were in full bloom, but the snow on the mountaintops had not yet melted, forming a poem.

In the Sanyo Road

In the morning, I caressed the pine trees on the top of Yongdusan Mountain. In the evening, the train departed from Shimonoseki under a covered sky. I sat tightly with my jacket on, passing the long evening. The moon was bright, flying tracelessly for a thousand miles. The border between heaven and man can be observed. The sea country is in deep spring, but it is still cold. Cherry blossoms are below the mountain, and snow is above it. The red makeup and white hair are pleasing to the eye.

The Rotary Club

Hawthorne's Transposition Case (22) 171

— Cheng Xiaoqing

I shifted my gaze and stared. It was also a Chinese person, wearing a black robe, very tall. This person accidentally turned his face, and I recognized him as that hateful and pitiful Qiu Kui. I was about to ask the question, "How is he here too?" Hawthorne suddenly said softly, "Don't ask yet. Now, try to use your gaze again and look at the outer corner on the left side of this wide room. Are there any people you recognize there?" I followed his instructions and looked far away. I saw that in the corner facing outwards on the left, there were also two local diners. One was a man and one was a woman. The woman was wearing a light yellow qipao, with black butterflies embroidered on the hem. Her hair was permed and unusually fluffy. This kind of dress was the most popular in Shanghai at that time. Her face was also very beautiful. She was looking down and talking and laughing with the man opposite her. The man was wearing a chestnut-colored suit, and his shiny hair was combed back very neatly. He had a tilted face, pressing close to the woman, with a flattering smile on his face. I looked again carefully. His nose was hooked, and his eyes were angular, which could not help but shock me. I said to Hawthorne in a low voice, "Is that Che Shijie?" Hawthorne winked at me and replied, "Why do you need to call him by name?" I was suddenly filled with anger and unconsciously moved my chair a little, preparing to stand up. Hawthorne said again, "What are you planning to do? Are you going to act? I advise you to calm down and think about your own position." Although I was stopped by Hawthorne's words, I could not restrain my anger. I wished I could rush forward and slap the villain in the face. Hawthorne said to me again in a low voice, "Calm down and look at them again." I turned my face and saw another peculiar action. The scheming young man was taking out a small violet velvet box, smiling and handing it to the woman opposite him. The woman opened the velvet box and looked at it carefully. A charming smile appeared on her face. I suddenly heard Hawthorne say to himself, "That's probably a ring. Including the velvet box, it's worth two or three dollars." I knew that our previous conjecture had been confirmed. The villain was indeed deceiving the woman with false pretenses. Before I could reply, I saw Qiu Kui from the next table turn his head and ask Hawthorne, "You called me here. What exactly is the matter?" Hawthorne also turned his body a little and replied, "According to you, you were not colluding with the traitor that night. Then, if you saw him, how would you deal with him?"

Grain, Foreign, and Ke Xin Rice All Fell 193

Following Du Mi, They Fell a Bit. The Price of Ke Xin Rice Dropped a Little over One Jiao.

The Price of Foreign Rice Dropped a Little over 0.05 Yuan

Yesterday, the price of Ke Xin rice was still not good. After the prosperity from the river reached its peak, people's expectations had already weakened. Therefore, the market had been stagnant the day before yesterday. Yesterday, as the price of Du Mi dropped by a little over 0.02 or 0.03 yuan, the appetite in this street was even weaker. As a result, the owners voluntarily lowered the price for disposal, and about 1,400 bags were traded. The price was down a little over 0.15 yuan from the previous day, with asking prices ranging from 11.28 yuan to 10.095 yuan. There were no other transactions. Since the price of gold had increased, it was difficult for the price of foreign rice to be close, and the Shanghai market was weak, the importers were very discouraged. Yesterday, there was only a small amount of round-trip turnover of about 200 tons, with the June price being 5.3 taels, down a little over 0.05 yuan from the previous opening price.

Flour Prices Slipped Slightly 194

Yesterday in the flour market, after the opening prices were set in the morning and afternoon, the market prices of each month generally trended towards a circling and flat decline. The quoted price of foreign wheat fell by about 0.03 or 0.04 yuan. Although it rained the night before, it was already clear yesterday, and most people seemed to be easing up. Generally, the floating amount had gradually shifted towards observation because the degree of increase had been considerable in the past few days of the week due to the circumstances. The situation for this month was still stable as the manufacturers had slightly increased their intake. Future months showed a soft trend as the customer gangs' thoughts were very weary, and many withdrew. In the future, it would be wise to temporarily set the trend, as the weather is still difficult to be optimistic about. As a result, the price for this month fell by 0.005 yuan compared to the previous day. June fell by 0.01 yuan, July fell by 0.0075 yuan, and August, September, and October fell by 0.0025 yuan.

Wheat Market Firm in the Near Term, Flat in the Distant Term 195

Yesterday, in the futures wheat market, after the opening prices were set in the morning and afternoon, the market prices of each month presented a phenomenon of being firm in the near term and flat in the distant term. Due to some traders being long on the current month, they had quite a bit of manipulation, so the market atmosphere was consistently firm and had a continuing upward trend, and the operators of the current months, had the bulk of the volume locked away, so the outside shorts were difficult to shake off. As for the various months in the distant term, the weather had turned clear, and the quoted price of foreign wheat had also decreased slightly, so there was a flat and soft trend. However, there would be many changes in the future if the new wheat harvest was not good. As a result, this month was 0.05 yuan better than the previous day, June was a little over 0.03 yuan lower, July and August were a little over 0.02 yuan lower, September was a little over 0.01 yuan lower, and October was a little over 0.02 yuan lower.

Silk, Tea, and Foreign Firms: Silk Market Prices Slightly Halted 196

Yesterday, the trading of silk by foreign firms in this port came to a complete standstill. The prices of silk in Europe, the United States, and China had fallen sharply, and the telegraphic transfer prices were surprisingly low. The losses for Chinese merchants were extremely large, making it difficult to sell. The market was holding its breath. Yesterday's silk dealers all had activity but no sales.

Most of the New Cocoons in Chang'an Have Thin Skins 197

The Unified Tugging is Only 30% As Good As In Prior Years... Cocoon Prices Have Already Risen to 50 Yuan In the villages near Chang'an, this year's early silkworms have suffered from the weather, and the late silkworms have been harmed by the severe cold and continuous rain. During the big sleep, 60-70% of the silkworms were discarded. New cocoons have already been put on the market, but the cocoon shops are only open to a little less than one-third of capacity. The number of goods arriving on the market is few. The unified tugging is only 30% as good as in prior years, and the quality of the cocoons is not good. Most of them have thin skins. Because of the rain, the arrival of goods on the market yesterday was even scarcer. The prices for high-quality cocoons have already opened at 50 yuan.

Chunmee from Suian Has Already Opened 198

Yesterday, in the foreign firm tea market in this port, the new offers for Chunmee green tea from Suian, coming from the estates of firms such as Jinlong and Jardine Matheson, were formally opened at 125 taels, which was 10 taels higher than last year. However, the harvest from each region this year was poor, and the sales of the tea shops were huge, which increased the cost accordingly. Furthermore, the domestic Chunmee has fallen by 10-20 taels recently, and the sales are still not very smooth. It seems difficult to regard the green tea market trend as optimistic. The Yingde firms and other estates of Qimen black tea were still sparing no effort in searching and buying in the market yesterday. Because the arrival of goods has been scarce recently, the attitude of Chinese merchants has been hardening, and the market has been able to hold its ground fairly well. The offer from Jardine Matheson for Hekou black tea yesterday was 75 taels, which was over 20 taels higher than last year. However, this area does not produce much tea, and the supply cannot meet the demand. In the current tea market trend, black tea seems to be better than green tea.

The Tea Market in Wubei is Bustling 199

The new teas from Wuyi have been discussed and priced by various firms for days, with dozens of offers every day. The mountain households are separated from the discussions, and there are not many deals that are opened. Until today (15th), although the tea guests from the east, west, south, and north are discussing prices, there is not a single place where the scale has been opened. Only the tea shops in the north have opened their scales today, and the number of people running around to various villages to search for goods is actually more than the number of crucian carp crossing the river. In the area around Xichongyuan, there are as many as 40-50 traders gathering to discuss prices. A single tea is discussed, and the shares are divided among several firms. It is estimated that the villages where the scales have been opened today include Wang Village, Dawuqian, Changrao, Jiang Village, Changtan, Longteng, and more than a dozen others, with prices ranging from 42 to 45 yuan per load. Because each of the above villages had mountain households who suffered from the pain of delayed sales at lower prices last year, they did not want to insist on discussion prices excessively and repeat the mistakes. They are all willing to dispose of the goods early. Based on the current market trend, it has become lively. There are also some wealthy merchants who, in light of the tender goods and low prices of this year's tea leaves, have temporarily formed shops. It is estimated that the recent additions include two in Fengshan, two in Tuokou, one in Xigu, and one in Zhongyun. (16th)

The Tea Market in Dewan is Affected by Bandits 200

The new teas from Dexing and Wannian are in the peak season for entering the market. However, recently, there have been bandits harassing the border area of ​​Le De again, and the villages and towns newly built in Haikou are panicked. The tea shops that are opening to collect tea in De have stopped their activity. The tea merchants from Wuyuan are also mostly hesitant to move forward, and the tea market has come to a standstill. Because the bandits are causing trouble everywhere, it is difficult for mountain households to feel at ease in picking and producing new tea from Wannian, and most of the households will allow the leaves to become old on the trees, which has greatly reduced the amount of production. In addition, since the tea leaves in this area have always been inferior, there are few people who collect tea leaves, and the market is even more depressed. (16th)

The Reasons for the Price Drop of Cotton Fabrics 201

The prices of woolen goods and cotton fabrics have been steadily falling recently. As the exchange rate has become tighter, the import cost of cotton fabrics has increased instead of decreasing. The selling price should logically increase, but the demand is weak, making it difficult to raise the price. The reasons for the repeated price drops, according to the investigation, are that a large number of cotton fabrics from Hong Kong and Dalian have been shipped to Shanghai in the past month. The selling prices are more than one point cheaper than in Shanghai. This is because imports from these two ports can avoid tariffs. This is why the market price of cotton fabrics in this port has become weak.

Rebar Turns Strong from Weak 202

After the outlet for rebar was dismal, the market situation was exceptionally idle. The standards fell again and again, so the lowest price was estimated to be 93 taels per ton. In recent days, the exchange rate has tended to decrease, people's sentiments have returned, and the selling price has increased. It is estimated that it can be sold for up to 95 taels per ton. It is estimated that the number of bars in the market yesterday was 600-700 tons, which were bought by construction workers. The export gangs such as the Yangtze River and inland river ports have also shipped goods.

Galvanized Iron Increases by 0.01 Yuan 203

The recent trading of 36-inch and 37-inch Dongyang galvanized iron has been very lively, but the amount of goods on the market is limited. After the goods were collected, the scarcity became even more apparent. Therefore, the standards have increased by 0.01 yuan. The selling price of 37-inch galvanized iron is 1.26 taels per sheet, and the selling price of 36-inch galvanized iron is 1.06 taels per sheet. According to the investigation, there were 4,000-5,000 sheets in transactions in the market yesterday. The buyers were all from the Yangtze River gang, and other gangs only had a few transactions.

[Resumption of Business in the Concessions P] 204

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce, after receiving an official letter from the Municipal Finance Bureau requesting it to find ways to persuade the fresh meat industry to resume business, yesterday convened a meeting of representatives from the fresh meat trade association, presided over by Chairman Wang Xiaolai and Executive Committee members Wang Yansong and Zheng Chengqing. U.S. Export Statistics for March

The U.S. Consulate General in this city has released figures for exports from all of China and Hong Kong to the United States for March. The value of goods for which consulate invoices were filed totaled US$1,013,670. The total for the first three months of this year is US$3,704,702. Textiles and raw materials accounted for the largest share, with exports valued at US$513,126 in March and US$2,379,978 for the first three months. Non-edible animal products were second, with exports valued at US$308,875 in March and US$775,917 for the first three months. The remaining exports were of much smaller value, not exceeding several tens of thousands of US dollars in March. However, according to new regulations by the U.S. Treasury Department, only goods subject to ad valorem duties now require consulate invoices. The consulate is unable to collect statistics for goods that are duty-free or subject to special taxes in the United States. Therefore, the aforementioned export figures do not represent the entirety of our country's exports to the United States.

Sixth District Party Headquarters Supports Abolition of Unequal Treaties Declaration

According to the Guomin News Agency, the Sixth District Party Headquarters declared: (Abridged) Our nation's survival does not depend on perfect territories, but is controlled by foreign aggressors of political or economic aggression. Thus, every blade of grass and every tree of ours, no matter what, is flesh on the knives of imperialists. Every thread and every building of ours, no matter which end, is an adornment of blue-eyed boys or purple-skirted attendants. But let us ask, why is our solemn and brilliant Chinese civilization reduced to remnants below the eighteenth level of hell today? If we think about it even a little, anyone can say in unison, this is thanks to the blessings of unequal treaties. Therefore, our nation's poverty and weakness are absolutely not the result of famines or internal strife, but rather the crystallization of what has been left by unequal treaties. From this, we know that the existence of unequal treaties is by no means a matter of individual honor or disgrace, but rather a watershed between the rise and fall of the Republic of China. Moreover, it is not only a small key to a nation's survival, but also the only fuse for East Asian security and global order. If we continue to tolerate them and allow them to continue to exist, not only will our descendants be slaves, accumulating contracts of servitude for countless kalpas, but our East Asian situation and world trends will also suffer serious collateral damage due to the disappearance of our national spirit. Therefore, our abolition of unequal treaties is neither making a merciless conflict with imperialists, nor is it an attempt to exploit a topic with the ambition to invade the world, but rather it is completely standing on the level playing field of international equality and demanding a self-determined path of national independence, political independence, and economic independence. We deeply know that selfish and self-interested imperialists may not respect our popular will and follow the trend of the world, and have the determination to voluntarily abandon unequal treaties. Therefore, we really have no second way except to save ourselves from danger, save ourselves from destruction, and free ourselves from shackles. Now, how fortunate that our National Congress can promote the indomitable national spirit under the guidance of the blue and white banner,

so that the intangible prison that the public has suffered for decades can have the possibility of restoring freedom through the blowing of this abolition of unequal treaties declaration. What a happy thing this is. However, the abolition of inequality in words alone may still be insufficient to seize the fierce flames of the strong. Therefore, we further hope that the diplomatic authorities will carry out the proposition of abolishing the treaty based on the public opinion of the people. At the same time, we also hope that the government and the public will work together and not let the five minutes of enthusiasm retain this bloody title for a long time. Minutes of the Shanghai Municipal Council Meeting

Approval of Municipal Chinese Advisor and Chinese Affairs Assistant

The Public Concession Shanghai Municipal Council, at its regular meeting on Wednesday, decided to appoint Wu Jingxiong as Municipal Advisor and He Dekui as Chinese Affairs Assistant, which was reported in the previous newspaper. The Municipal Council officially released the minutes of the meeting yesterday, with the details as follows:

Water Supply Expert

Those present at the meeting were Chairman Macnaghten, Vice-Chairman Sperling, and directors Peel, Bland, Carneck, Fukushima, Xu Xinliu, Xu Shi, Okamoto, Raven, Hu Mengjia, Yuan Ludeng, Yu Qiaqing, as well as Secretary-General Fessenden and Acting Secretary-General Mackie. Macnaghten presided over the meeting and first reported that he had received a telegram from water supply expert Schell, informing him that he could not leave the United States before August 15. The Municipal Council immediately telegraphed back, urging him not to postpone his trip beyond August 15 and asking him to telegraph the exact date of his arrival in Shanghai.

Implementation of Factory Law

Next, the issue of implementing factory regulations in the concessions was discussed. Secretary-General Fessenden read a letter from the Senior Consul and the Municipal Council's reply, and reported to the board that the Chinese authorities had invited three experts from the League of Nations in Geneva to come to Shanghai to study the regulations and their implementation.

Appointment of Chinese Staff

Finally, the chairman reported that a special committee had met on Monday and unanimously decided that the Municipal Council should appoint two senior Chinese staff members: one as Municipal Advisor and one as Chinese Assistant Secretary. Regarding the candidates for Municipal Advisor and Chinese Affairs Assistant, although many people had submitted letters of recommendation to the Municipal Council, the Chinese directors unanimously recommended Dr. Wu Jingxiong to take on the position of Municipal Advisor. Although Mr. Wu did not submit a letter of recommendation himself, he had served as a judge and acting president of the Provisional Court and was well-qualified. The Chinese directors also recommended Mr. He Dekui as Chinese Assistant Secretary. The matter was then discussed and approved.

Shanghai Coal Industry Appeals on Behalf of Shandong Mining Merchants

Request to Order Jiaoji Railway to Cancel Price Increase

The Coal Industry Association sent a telegram to the Ministry of Railways: "To Minister of the Ministry of Railways in Nanjing: We have recently received a telegram from the Shandong Zibo and Weifang Mining Coal Industry Association stating that the Jiaoji Railway, in terms of mining coal freight rates, disregards the development of national coal, does not care about the life and death of miners, and ignores all interests, resolutely deciding to suddenly increase mining coal freight rates by 40% in just two years, forcing the mining industry to be unable to support itself. Therefore, the Shandong Zibo and Weifang mining coal industries convened a general meeting and decided to temporarily suspend operations on May 21 to await further orders, and telegraphed for assistance, etc., which has arrived in Shanghai. Upon investigation, when the Jiaoji Railway increased prices last year, our association duly requested the restoration of the old regulations to facilitate coal transportation and received approval No. 591, stating that the Jiaoji Railway Management Committee submitted a report stating that the supply and demand of coal in various parts of Shandong Province have been corresponding in recent months and that the coal and coke freight rates of the railway have been restored on November 1, and the ministry issued instructions to approve the record. With this approval, coal merchants celebrated that the government could adopt public opinions and that the development of mining merchants was promising. Unexpectedly, the ink was not yet dry, and in an instant, there was an increase of 20% on May 1 this year. Our association has already submitted a request to exempt the increase on May 4 to encourage mining merchants and facilitate sales, and two weeks have passed, but there has been no reply. The fear of danger and doubt is always in our minds. Now, unfortunately, Shandong mines have suspended operations, which means that tens of millions of lives along the Jiaoji Railway line will be trapped at the same time, and the severity of the disaster cannot be described in words. Even more unfortunately, Shandong mines did not suspend operations during the warlord era, nor did they suspend operations during the war, but they suspended operations at the moment when military administration was unified and the people's assembly closed. It is truly a shocking innovation. How can all our citizens ignore it? All members of our association, who are engaged in coal, have a close relationship with coal mining merchants, and if we do not urgently make a plea for survival, we are sitting idly by while Shandong mines and tens of millions of lives along the Jiaoji Railway line are trapped in desperation. In the event that national coal is cut off, the industrial, commercial, and transportation sectors must completely demand foreign coal to maintain operations, and economic leakage will be even worse than before, and the industrial plan will be hopeless. Looking at the future, the hidden worries are extremely deep. We hereby telegraphed to appeal, requesting your ministry to take care of the people's suffering, urgently provide relief, and immediately order the Jiaoji Railway authorities to cancel the price increase and persuade the mining merchants to resume operations to stabilize the miners and maintain the status quo. As for the railway's income problem, we request that the railway be ordered to prepare more vehicles and transport as much as possible, so the income will be abundant and the economy will be prosperous. The above requests are all urgently awaiting your approval. Salutations from the Shanghai Coal Industry Association."

Request Exemption of Business Tax for Western-Style Machine-Made Goods

Shanghai Machinery Association Sends Telegram to Ministry of Finance

The Shanghai Association of Machine-Made National Goods Factories yesterday sent a document to the Ministry of Finance requesting exemption from business tax for machine-made Western-style goods, stating: "Regarding the matter of machine-made Western-style goods that have been approved for exemption from business tax, in the late Qing Dynasty, there were precedents for reducing or exempting taxes and customs duties. On June 11 of the ninth year of the Republic of China, the Taxation Department of the former Beijing government jointly formulated nine articles of the current method of taxing machine-made Western-style goods, and Article 2 of Chapter 1 was added in February of the thirteenth year of the Republic of China to show restrictions. It has been used for more than ten years, so recently the number of factories manufacturing machine-made Western-style goods has gradually increased, and imported goods among daily necessities have gradually decreased. Inspecting the 'General Situation of Shanghai Industry' compiled and printed by the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs, which details the development statistics of machine factories, we know the reasons. First, it is due to the government's preferential treatment for machine-made goods, giving various conveniences to machine-made national goods factories; second, it is due to the success of the Xinhai Revolution, which allowed the people to recover from poverty and strive for the development of national goods; third, it is due to the opportunity of the European War, when foreign goods were unable to come, so national goods could develop freely and gain the trust of the people. From the end of the Guangxu period to the 17th year of the Republic of China, the establishment of machine factories has increased from dozens of factories to 1,441 factories, which is clear evidence. Recently, due to the government's revision of the tax system, the abolition of all customs duties, and the revision of import and export taxes, each province and city collects business tax to compensate for the deficit. Among the small tax items, there is a provision for collecting 0.2% of business tax for manufacturing industries, such as papermaking, cotton textiles, hemp textiles, box making, enamelware, etc., which are all machine-made goods. Upon investigation, machine-made goods were originally imitated to resist the invasion of foreign goods, and most of their raw materials still rely on imports, which have already borne heavy central taxes, so their enjoyment of reduced or exempted other taxes and fees is also a deserved benefit. Although customs duties have recently been abolished, if business tax is levied again, the benefits enjoyed by the machine-made industry for decades will be abolished at once, and the young industry will inevitably be unable to bear the burden. Taking Shanghai as an example, a detailed statistical review of the capital of 1,441 machine factories of Chinese merchants shows that the wealth is not as good as the capital of 56 machine factories of Japanese residents, which can be seen in general. How to work hard to improve and how to maintain it without collapse are still without a decision to follow. Today, with the increase in the burden of business tax, the collapse of Chinese merchant factories can be expected. Moreover, since business tax is used to compensate for customs duties, machine-made goods should be exempt from customs duties according to the original plan, and business tax should be exempted in principle to show fairness. Therefore, we specially submit this request, hoping that your ministry will approve the exemption of business tax according to the previous examples of preferential treatment for machine factories, so as to protect and promote it, which is truly a matter of public convenience. Respectfully submitted."

Restriction on Special Tax Collection for Silk Bonds

Request Only Levy Factory-Run Silk

Exempt from Raw Silk, etc.

The issuance of 8 million yuan in Jiangsu-Zhejiang silk industry bonds has been announced and implemented by the National Government's Executive Yuan. The Ministries of Finance and Industry have separately appointed Mu Ouchu, Zou Bingwen, Song Ziliang, etc., as members of the committee in charge of allocating bond amounts and managing funds. They are preparing to jointly organize a specialized committee with representatives from silk factories and financial circles in the three regions of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Shanghai to carry out the project. However, the committee regulations and implementation details have been drafted and agreed upon by the Ministries of Finance and Industry and submitted to the Executive Yuan for review. Since the National Congress has just closed, it must wait until next Tuesday to be submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval and promulgation before the committee members can follow them. The Jianghai Customs has been ordered by the Ministry of Finance to collect a special tax of 30 yuan per dan of yellow and white silk exported from Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces starting from the 20th of this month to be allocated to the Jiangsu-Zhejiang silk industry bond fund. This has caused panic among silk merchants in Jili, Zhejiang Province. The issuance of 8 million yuan in Jiangsu-Zhejiang silk industry bonds is only to provide relief to factory-run silk businesses in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces and has nothing to do with silk merchants in Jili and other places. It is inappropriate to include yellow and white silk from Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces in the customs' collection of heavy taxes. Therefore, Shen Huachen, chairman of the specialized committee for relief to silk factory businesses in the three regions of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Shanghai, has now submitted a request to the Ministry of Finance to clearly stipulate that a special tax of 30 yuan per dan will be collected for yellow and white factory-run silk exported from Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, and raw silk, etc., will be exempt from the tax to avoid confusion.

Zhejiang Box Tea Begins Transport to Shanghai

Box tea produced in Jinqu, Yan, Shangjiang, and other places in Zhejiang Province has been transported to Shanghai by the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway for export overseas. This year's new box tea has now been put on the market for transportation. Yesterday, 1,024 boxes of new box tea were transported by the Lubao Shuntai Transfer Company in Zhabei. Municipal Chamber of Commerce Protects Tung Oil Export Sales

Request to Reduce Export Tax Rate

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the Ministry of Finance: "To the Ministry of Finance in Nanjing: On the 21st of this month, we received a letter from the Shanghai Oil and Hemp Industry Association stating that the new export tariff rates announced by the Ministry of Finance estimate the taxable price of tung oil at 210.99, and the tax rate is 7.5%, with a levy of 1 tael and 6 qian of Customs silver. It is noted that the valuation is based on the value in 1929. The original export tariff rates estimated the taxable price of tung oil at 6 taels, with a tax rate of 5%, amounting to a levy of 3 qian of Customs silver, plus a 2.5% surtax of 1 qian and 5 fen, totaling 4 qian and 5 fen of silver. Now that the surtax has been removed, the regular tax has actually increased to 2.56 times, which is shocking. Moreover, it is unfair to use the highest price in 1929 as the tax standard. At a time when export business is declining, the sudden increase in tax rates is unbearable for merchants. Our association believes that there is a need for revision. We have already telegraphed the Ministry of Finance to revise the tax rates lightly and re-estimate the taxable prices. We have always admired your association as the hub of the city's commerce and have conveyed the letter accordingly. Please forward it to the Ministry of Finance to revise the tax rules, which is a matter of public gratitude, and copy the original telegram to the association. Upon investigation, the sale of tung oil abroad has always been dominated by our country's products in the market. Since Americans planted tung trees in their own country to resist it, the annual production has increased dramatically, from 1,700 tons to 15,000 tons. It can be predicted that the future sales of Chinese tung oil abroad will be invaded by Indian and Ceylon products, and American tung oil will be fiercely competitive. Thereafter, the market price will only tend to fall, and there is no reason to return to the prosperity of 1929. The new tax rules, which are more than 2.5 times heavier than the old ones, will inevitably lead to increased costs in foreign trade and make it more difficult. According to the letter, it is reasonable to telegraph your ministry to assess the situation. Please consider that our country's export of tung oil is no longer comparable to the exclusive market a few years ago, and try to protect it. Re-evaluate and revise this export tariff rate, or change the ad valorem tax to a quantity tax, so as to suit the current market situation and not cause excessive burden on exporters. The national economy and people's livelihood will benefit. Salutations from the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce."

Shanghai Liquor Inspection Office Restored

Director Song Jiju Has Taken Office

The Shanghai Liquor Inspection Office, formerly attached to the Second District Tobacco and Alcohol Bureau of Jiangsu Province, was virtually eliminated after the bureau was abolished. Now, the Ministry of Finance has found that the inspection office has been effective since its establishment and that the inspection should be restored as counterfeit liquor is harming public health. Therefore, the Jiangsu Stamp and Alcohol Bureau has ordered the Shanghai Stamp Tax Bureau Director Song Jiju to concurrently serve as the Director of the Liquor Inspection Office, and he took office the day before yesterday and has dispatched personnel to conduct inspections.

Shanghai County's rural clearance affairs have expired after three months. Liu Shufan, Director of the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau, took leave to visit his sick mother in Fujian Province. The bureau affairs were handled by Associate Director Shen Shuyu. The bureau has been in constant contact with him by letter and telegram. Recently, a telegram from him stated that his mother's illness has turned for the better and is expected to recover. He plans to return to the bureau to cancel his leave on the next available ship and will arrive in Shanghai within a few days.

Drug Resistance Association Prepares for June 3rd Anniversary

June 3rd is the 92nd anniversary of the ban on opium by our country's drug resistance pioneer Lin Zexu. The year before last, Wang Jingqi, chairman of the China National Drug Resistance Association, submitted a request to the National Government to designate this day as the Anti-Smoking Memorial Day to show commendation. The National Government issued a circular to all provinces, cities, and counties, ordering them to convene local organizations and groups on this day every year to hold commemorations to show commendation and encourage them. Over the years, the association has issued circulars to local drug resistance organizations to jointly prepare for the event with local party and government agencies. As the date of the memorial is approaching, the association specially formulated a plan yesterday and sent it to various places, ordering them to prepare quickly and hold the event on schedule, and made a large number of propaganda materials to meet the needs of local commemorations. In addition, Shanghai is the focus of attention at home and abroad, and it is not enough to hold a large-scale event to show our country's determination to resist drugs. The association specially sent personnel to the Shanghai Municipal Party Department and the Municipal Government yesterday to discuss joint preparations, and the results were very satisfactory. A meeting of representatives of various legal entities will be convened within a few days to join the preparations so that it can be held on a large scale at that time.

Local News from This City

Counterfeit Customs Treasury Bills Discovered on the Market

Eighteenth-Year Customs Treasury Bills

Exquisitely Printed, Almost Indistinguishable from Genuine Bills

Police Have Already Arrested Two People

Confessions Indicate the Bills Came from Xiangtan

Since the National Government established its capital in Nanjing, five years have passed. However, due to frequent internal disturbances over the years, coupled with the simultaneous launch of various construction projects, the need for funds is pressing, and the treasury is empty. To avoid having nothing to cook with, the only plan is to issue national bonds to provide financial support. Therefore, the bonds issued successively over the years have numerous names. Although the amount is no less than several thousand million, the payment of interest and repayment of principal have never been delayed, the fund is stable, and the management is proper. As a result, credit is evident, the market is circulating, and no accidents have occurred. However, recently, some traitors, only seeking private gain and disregarding national credit, dared to counterfeit the eighteenth-year Customs Treasury Bills for deceptive use. The financial authorities were not initially aware of it until Renyi Money Shop in this city received two of these bills, worth two yuan each, sent from Bengbu, and transferred them to Wang Dazong, an official of the Central Bank, for identification. After confirming that they were counterfeit, he reported to the president, who submitted it to the Ministry of Finance. Only then did they learn that counterfeit bills had been discovered outside. Therefore, the Ministry of Finance issued a circular to the Central, China, and Communications Banks, informing branches in various locations to pay attention to the matter and to secretly investigate the counterfeiters. Once they were found, they were to be arrested and severely punished. As for the counterfeit bills discovered this time, according to detailed identification by the Customs Office of the Ministry of Finance, the printing was very exquisite, and the colors and patterns on both sides of the bills were no different from genuine bills. However, upon closer inspection, the Chinese characters on the front of the counterfeit bills were slightly different from those on the genuine bills. Without this flaw, the counterfeit bills could have been mistaken for genuine bills, and it would have been difficult to distinguish between them. After receiving this news, the silver and money industry and the securities market began to pay close attention to the eighteenth-year Customs Treasury Bills. However, on the afternoon of the day before yesterday, Luo Yizhai, an accountant from Yiqingxiang, a shop located at 366 Taipingfang, Hankou Road, also ordered a tea servant named Yao Amao to take sixteen of these counterfeit bills to the Bank of China to exchange for 32 yuan in cash. After the bank staff discovered it, they reported it to the General Patrol Room, which dispatched Detective Wu Chunrong to arrest Yao along with the counterfeit bills. Then they arrested Yao. Yesterday morning, they escorted them to the Special District Local Court. Wang Yaotang, a police lawyer, charged Luo and Yao with forgery of documents under Article 233, Paragraph 3 of the Criminal Law. Zhao Songlu, specially dispatched by the Customs Office, went to court to explain in detail the differences between the genuine and counterfeit bills. Luo confessed that the bills were sent by a Mr. Wen from the Tongqingxiang Silk Shop in Xiangtan, who entrusted him to cash them. He has now telegraphed to inquire about their origin and has hired lawyer Fan Gang to defend him. Judge Xu instructed both defendants to be remanded in custody and rescheduled the trial for seven days. According to Zhao's statement in court, the counterfeit bills were manufactured very exquisitely, and one would be fooled if they were not careful. If they had not been in circulation for long, there would be no major harm. On the contrary, the number of people who might be fooled and suffer losses could be considerable.

Postal Service Dismisses Employee for Forging Receipts and Committing Fraud

Soliciting Parcel Postages

Carrying Back for Embezzlement

Li Zuoming, a native of Ningbo, used to work in the parcel department of the Post Office. Later, he was dismissed by the director for dereliction of duty and has been unemployed since then. Over the years, his livelihood has become extremely difficult, so he resorted to illegal activities. He rented a room on the second floor of No. 31 Qipu Road, soliciting parcel postages from various shops. According to the articles mailed, the procedures were complicated, and unless one was skilled, errors would occur. Li had been in this business for a long time and was not only familiar with the matter but also proficient in the way to commit fraud. Therefore, after receiving a parcel for mailing, he would often carry it back to his residence and examine the type of goods. If it was necessary to pay customs duties, he would affix a customs duty form that he had forged to the package and then mail it. He would also overreport the fees to the consignor and pocket the proceeds. This kind of fraudulent act has now been detected by the Post Office, and they have sent inspectors to conduct a thorough investigation. The day before yesterday, it was finally found out, and the Hongkou Patrol Room was notified, and Detectives Mao Yiwen and Bao Tan Hechengrui went to Li's residence. At that time, Li was writing a counterfeit receipt, and his friend Xu Linxiang, a shop assistant from a stationery store at No. 84 Qipan Street, was sitting next to Li, holding a genuine receipt from the Post Office so that Li could imitate it. Shui Quanxiang, an employee of Yuantai Forwarding Company at No. 386 Shanxi Road, was also arrested because he sent goods to Li's place and asked Li to mail them on his behalf. Li confessed to forging the tax-paid slip and other details and confessed that the fake seal was hidden at No. 107 O' Jia Road, and the receipt was entrusted to Xieqing Printing House at No. 94 Datong Road, Zhabei. The detectives first went and took out the seal, and then went to the printing house for a search, but the owner had already fled. Yesterday morning, the police escorted Li and the other three people and various forged items to the Special District Local Court. Judge Xiao interrogated them. Police lawyer Li Zhishan stated the circumstances of the case and presented the items seized. Among them was a receipt with the freight fee filled in for 19 yuan and 5 jiao. However, according to the weight of the goods, it would only cost 7 yuan and 5 jiao to mail it directly to the Post Office. From this one point, it can be seen that Li's income was not enough. Later, according to Li's confession, because he could not make a living, he used this to make a small profit. Xu confessed that he asked Li for a debt of two yuan, and he did not participate in Li's fraud and hired lawyer Jiang Yiping to defend him. Shui confessed that he was a friend of Li and just went to chat, which led to the implication. The judge ordered the three defendants to be remanded in custody and rescheduled the hearing.

Further Hearing in the Ni Guangxun Missing Person Property Dispute Case

Court Orders Reconciliation within Two Weeks

After the disappearance of Ni Guangxun, a student at Chih Tze University, Fan Abao, who used to be a kitchen maid in the Ni family, claimed to be Guangxun's wife and filed a lawsuit against Ni's sister, Ni Zengshi, for occupying Guangxun's family property. The Special District Local Court summoned the defendant, who hired lawyers Zhang Deqin and Shen Yuesheng to defend and absolutely denied that Abao was his sister-in-law and that he had occupied his brother's property. Abao then asked Ni Guangxun's uncle, Ni Wenming, to be brought to court, which could prove it. The judge ordered the plaintiff to pay additional litigation fees and wait for Ni Wenming to be brought to court for questioning. This has been reported in the previous two newspapers. Yesterday was the date for the continued hearing of the case. Ni Wenming did not obey the summons to appear in court, but only sent a letter and sent someone to the court. The letter generally stated that he was old and sick, closed his door to recuperate, and could not move, so it was difficult to obey the order to appear in court for confrontation. As for the point of contention in this case, according to what he knew, Guangxun had three brothers, and Guangxun was the youngest and had not been formally married. When Guangxun's father died, he made a will distributing the property to his sons. He did not know whether Guangxun's share had been used up for his studies because he had lived apart from them for more than 40 years. Therefore, the lawyers hired by the defendant, Zhang and Shen, claimed that what was stated in the letter was true, but the plaintiff still insisted on his previous claims and did not give in. Then, Judge Yang ordered the case to be rescheduled and advised the two parties to go out and reconcile within two weeks. If it is still not resolved when the deadline expires, the plaintiff should pay the litigation fees and wait for the hearing to continue.

Danyang Kidnappers Arrested in Shanghai

Li Wenxiang Allowed to Be Transferred to the Municipal Public Security Bureau

Kidnappers Zhou Yaoqi, Zhao Jintai, Li Wenxiang, etc., colluded with Shen Shanyuan in February this year to kidnap a five-year-old son surnamed Wang and a nine-year-old son surnamed Li from Danyang County and hid them in the Zhao bandit's house in Xinchangli, Hongkou. They also sent letters to the families of the two children, demanding ransom. The ransom was 10,000 yuan for Wang's child and 8,000 yuan for Li's child. The families received the letters and each sent someone to Shanghai to secretly negotiate at the Luoyanglou Teahouse near the North Railway Station. Because the amounts were very different, no agreement was reached. Recently, Shen Bandit has been arrested by the Danyang County Government and confessed that his accomplices were all hiding in Shanghai. The county government specially consulted the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau to investigate and arrest them. The day before yesterday, detectives arrested Zhou Bandit and went to the Harbin Patrol Room to secretly go to Xinchangli with Chinese and Western detectives to arrest Zhao Bandit and the two children. Unexpectedly, Zhao had already fled upon hearing the news, and the two children had also been abducted elsewhere. Later, Zhou Bandit was interrogated to find out the whereabouts of Li Bandit, who confessed that he lived at No. 7 Harbin Road. So the detective went to the Jing'an Temple Patrol Room at about 2:00 AM yesterday morning and worked with the detectives to go to arrest Li and Li's wife, Wei. Then, a suspect named Liu Dehuai was arrested in Xinchangli. They were all escorted to the Special District Local Court at 9:00 AM. Judge Ge interrogated them. Qin Bin, a detective from the Municipal Public Security Bureau, went to court to request extradition, while Zhang Tianyin, a police lawyer, stated that unless it was proven that Li Wenxiang was related to the kidnapping case, the police had objections to the extradition. Judge Ge questioned the defendants, who all denied kidnapping. As a result, Li Wenxiang was handed over to Qin Bin and taken to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for interrogation. Liu Dehuai and Li Wei were remanded in custody and ordered to submit additional evidence and reschedule the hearing.

Zhang Ji to Depart for Guangdong This Morning 205

The Elders Held Their Final Deliberation Last Night

Concrete Plan Handed to Zhang to Take to Guangdong

Wu Tiecheng Decided to Remain in Shanghai to Negotiate

Elders such as Zhang Jingjiang, Li Shizeng, and Cai Yuanpei have been in Shanghai for several days, discussing and mediating the Guangdong situation and peaceful resolution methods. After Zhang Ji, a member of the Central Supervisory Committee, arrived in Shanghai a few days ago, he immediately participated in the discussions. Last night, the elders held their final meeting at Zhang Jingjiang's residence, engaging in detailed discussions for several hours. A concrete plan has been agreed upon and handed to Zhang Ji to take to Guangdong to negotiate everything. Zhang Ji is scheduled to depart for Guangdong this morning at 8:00 AM aboard the French postal ship Sphinx. Wu Tiecheng will remain in Shanghai to negotiate. The details obtained by our newspaper's reporter are described below.

Shi Zeng Visits Zhang 206

Yesterday morning at around 11:00 AM, Li Shizeng visited Zhang Jingjiang's residence on Route Massenet for a detailed discussion on the Guangdong situation, which lasted for two hours before he left. At the same time, Wu Tiecheng and Zhang Ji also went to meet. It was agreed that they would gather at Zhang Jingjiang's residence at 6:00 PM in the evening for a final discussion on everything and to decide on concrete measures.

Final Meeting 207

Starting at 6:00 PM last night, cars jammed the entrance of Zhang's residence on Route Massenet. The elders who attended the meeting included Cai Yuanpei, Li Shizeng, Zhang Ji, Wu Tiecheng, and Minister of Industry Kong Xiangxi. Wang Chonghui did not attend. Zhang Jingjiang hosted a lavish banquet and immediately began detailed discussions. At 8:30 PM, Wu Tiecheng was the first to leave. Cai Yuanpei left at 9:00 PM. At 9:30 PM, Kong Xiangxi, Li Shizeng, Zhang Ji, and others left one after another. According to Kong, who spoke to our newspaper's reporter, there is a solution for the Guangdong situation, and regardless, it will not resort to military force.

Departure This Morning 208

Zhang Ji, a member of the Central Supervisory Committee, who bears the heavy responsibility of mediating the Guangdong situation, is scheduled to depart for Guangdong this morning at 8:00 AM aboard the French postal ship Sphinx. Wu Tiecheng told our newspaper's reporter yesterday that Zhang Puquan decided to depart for Guangdong tomorrow morning (i.e., this morning) to negotiate, while he will stay here to work on this and will not accompany Zhang.

Sun Ke Goes to Guangdong to Mediate 209

Chen Youren and His Wife Travel on the Same Ship

Obeying Central Government Orders to Explain in Person

Sun Ke, Minister of Railways, accompanied by his wife and several attendants, indeed departed for Guangdong on the Asama Maru of the Japan Mail Steamship Company at 4:30 AM the day before yesterday. Sun and others left their residence on Route Molière by car at 10:30 PM on the 20th and boarded the ship at the Huishan Wharf at around 11:00 PM. Also traveling to Guangdong on the same ship were former Foreign Minister Chen Youren and his wife. Chen had been staying at the Claremont Hotel at the western end of Route Lafayette and Rue Pichon in Shanghai. According to the hotel's servants, Mr. and Mrs. Chen had been staying there for about three months and only moved out on the evening of the 20th, taking a car to the Huishan Wharf to board the Asama Maru for Hong Kong. Our reporter especially visited Kong Xiangxi, Minister of Industry, who came to Shanghai to mediate the Guangdong situation. According to his conversation, Sun Zhesheng is very willing to mediate the Guangdong situation. Although he telegraphed Guangdong twice from Shanghai, asking them to consider the overall situation, he still felt that it would be difficult to quickly explain the talks unless he went to Guangdong in person to explain. The central government also expressed sympathy for this. Therefore, Sun's trip to Guangdong was actually dispatched by the central government and bears the responsibility of mediation.

City Chamber of Commerce

Inquiry about the End of May Closing Period 213

Telegram to the Ministry of Industry and the Bureau of Social Affairs

The City Chamber of Commerce yesterday sent a telegram to the Ministry of Industry of the Executive Yuan and the Bureau of Social Affairs of the city regarding the issue of the end of May closing period. The original telegram said: To the Ministry of Industry of the Executive Yuan in Nanjing, the Bureau of Social Affairs of Shanghai, In the case of the national calendar business community closing, according to previous reports, it has been approved by the Executive Yuan that closing at the end of May, the end of September will remain the same, and the annual grand closing will be extended to January 31 of the following year, etc. However, without an explicit order, they have never been followed. A telegram was sent to the Executive Yuan on the first day of this month, but no instructions were received. Now the end of May closing period is very near, and merchants in various industries in this city have repeatedly inquired, but they have no basis to answer. We hereby telegram again to ask for your consideration and expedite the telegram reply so that there is something to follow. Earnestly praying, Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce.

Sand and Gravel Industry Resumes Operations Yesterday 214

Request to Prohibit Illegal Levies

Waiting for Formal Cancellation

The work stoppage of the sand and gravel industry in this city ended yesterday with the full resumption of operations. A further account of the various circumstances is recorded below:

Full Resumption of Operations 215

The sand and gravel industry received a continued instruction the night before last from the Ministry of Finance, No. 1280, which has been formally consulted with the Zhejiang Provincial Government to transfer the order to cancel. All the operators in the industry believe that since the Ministry of Finance has already agreed, there should be no further changes in the future, and the work stoppage was also a last resort. Therefore, they unanimously resumed operations yesterday and are waiting for formal cancellation.

Report to the Authorities 216

After resuming operations yesterday, the sand and gravel industry also reported to the authorities, stating: "Reporting on the end of the work stoppage and requesting that the collection of sand and mud management fees, which are similar to disguised likin, be prohibited in order to maintain political order and ensure business stability. It has been reported that the office for issuing sand dredging permits, commissioned by the Construction Department of the Zhejiang Provincial Government, is levying sand and mud management fees, which are similar to disguised likin, in Jiangsu Province, causing a work stoppage. On May 20, we received a letter from the City Chamber of Commerce stating that the Construction Department of Zhejiang Province is levying sand and mud production and sales, which is a heavy burden on merchants, and requested that it be transferred and cancelled. We immediately telegraphed the Ministry of Finance to request that it be stopped. Now, we have received approval No. 12765 from the Ministry of Finance, stating that we have received the telegram and will consult the Zhejiang Provincial Government to investigate and cancel it. Please be informed. This approval, etc. Having received this, we will record and transfer the approval, hoping that you will investigate and comply. Also, Approval No. 12804 from the Ministry of Finance stated that we have received your report and have consulted the Zhejiang Provincial Government to request cancellation of the various sections stated. Please be informed. This approval, etc. Having received this, we immediately sent personnel to distribute notices to various places overnight, and all the operators in the industry were satisfied and resumed operations on the 21st. However, since this kind of exorbitant tax has been ordered to be cancelled by the ministry, it should be stopped from being collected. However, we have found that the office is still levying it, which is a disregard for political order and requires a request to stop it." Based on this, we hereby submit a document for your consideration, requesting that the collection of management fees similar to disguised likin be prohibited in order to maintain political order and ensure business stability. We hope that you will approve it for the public good.

Prohibit Illegal Levies 217

Yesterday, the guild received reports from more than 20 shipowners loading yellow sand from Zhujiajian, Qushan, and other places in Zhejiang Province for shipment to Shanghai, stating that the Dachang contractor in charge of donation taxes, due to the fierce opposition in Shanghai, had recently sent staff to Zhujiajian and other production areas to levy taxes. All loaded sand and gravel must first pay taxes before being allowed to pass. After receiving the report, the guild plans to telegram the Zhejiang Provincial Government to order a stop.

Concession Butchers to Open Today 218

Result of Persuasion by the City Chamber of Commerce

After the fresh meat industry in this city went on strike together due to the slaughter tax issue, the concession butchers have accepted the persuasion of the City Chamber of Commerce and are scheduled to open today and resume operations. The various situations obtained yesterday are recorded below:

No Meat Today 219

For the sake of aiding their counterparts in the northern and southern parts of the city, the fresh meat industry in the concessions implemented a work stoppage. The meat shops in the concessions completely sold out their stored meat yesterday. Today, no meat is available for sale in the Public Concession. The French Concession has also sold out. The Sanitation Department of the Public Concession and the French Concession and the City Public Security Bureau sent personnel to various shops yesterday to inquire about the latest situation.
